        <script type="application/ld+json">
[{"@context":{"@vocab":"https://schema.org","kg":"https://g.co/kg"},"@type":"WebPage","@id":"https://www.acronis.com/en/blog/posts/paradise-ransomware-strikes-again/#WebPage","name":"Acronis Blog","url":"https://www.acronis.com/en/blog/posts/paradise-ransomware-strikes-again/","publisher":{"@id":"https://www.acronis.com/en/company/","url":"https://www.acronis.com/en"},"headline":"Paradise Ransomware strikes again","description":"The Paradise strain of ransomware is back, launching a new round of attacks in January 2018. Here’s a detailed look at the threat and how to combat it."},{"@type":"Article","@context":{"@vocab":"https://schema.org","kg":"https://g.co/kg"},"@id":"https://www.acronis.com/en/blog/posts/paradise-ransomware-strikes-again/#Article","url":"https://www.acronis.com/en/blog/posts/paradise-ransomware-strikes-again/","publisher":{"@id":"https://www.acronis.com/#Organization"},"inLanguage":"en-US","headline":"Paradise Ransomware strikes again","mainEntityOfPage":"https://www.acronis.com/en/blog/posts/paradise-ransomware-strikes-again/","datePublished":"2018-01-22T18:12:39.000000Z","image":["https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/852dbe610ed1eb08f9294689b21d3044.jpg","https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/9c23fc2adfb317dc5147918746c1480f.jpg","https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/f3afc4c02f83032c7152f3ae595e6a00.jpg","https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/fa3ef6a6c7ad7b955e13213de0dc486f.jpg","https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/4524ea3e23370100e4d9818dc87cf26a.jpg","https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/c5084dbf116a9a692ba8028269027cc8.jpg","https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/bd41d9dffec2b9c9c831288f3d086fe6.jpg","https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/8886a42936068d3763cac785df815cd6.jpg","https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/74fc117da2186d7cdc0a2de9ac6ab388.jpg","https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/91ae29c1926bddedb4bc1ba72ecf03a2.jpg","https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/8cc965cc9d494f1b98f0d4ba67ce6dae.jpg","https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/dd62f7f5415bd0ff0d4a3b236c95052d.jpg","https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/30006408baf99b0276301a7be73d0f5f.jpg","https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/2439b612d979318255717cbefd37a204.jpg"],"articleBody":"<p>The Paradise ransomware that was active in September 2017 is back with a new round of attacks, starting at the beginning of January 2018. Leveraging the Ransomware as a Service (RaaS) model, the Paradise strain provides an unbreakable encryption scheme by using the RSA cipher for file encryption – which is an unusual cipher choice.</p><p>The ransomware’s executable file is archived and spread via spam email as a zip attachment. To become infected, a user opens the attachment, unpacks it, and executes the extracted application.</p><h3><span>Static Analysis</span></h3><p>The ‘DP_Main.exe’ ransomware file is a .NET compiled executable and requires .NET Framework 3.5 to start on a user’s machine (MD5: 8aa00ee509a649619794fc1390319293). The PE file is 36,684 bytes and was compiled on January 5, 2018.</p><h3><span>Installation</span></h3><p>The malware copies itself to the following folder on a user’s computer:</p><p><em>C:\\Users\\&lt;USER&gt;\\AppData\\Roaming\\DP\\</em></p><p>The executable adds the reference to itself in the Autorun Windows registry key as the following value:</p><p><em>‘DP_Main’ = ‘c:\\Users\\&lt;USER&gt;\\AppData\\Roaming\\DP\\DP_Main.exe’</em></p><h3><span>Key generation</span></h3><p>The <a href=\"https://www.acronis.com/en-us/ransomware-protection/\">ransomware</a> creates ‘DecryptionInfo.auth’ file in the following folders:</p><ul><li>%USER%\\</li><li>%USER%\\Desktop\\</li><li>&nbsp;Program Files\\</li></ul><p>The key file contains the session RSA private key in the XML format, encrypted with the master RSA public key and Base64 encoded:</p><p>The master RSA 1024-bit public key is hard coded in Base64:</p><p><em>&lt;RSAKeyValue&gt;Modulus&gt;um4QYAdi0y8L+VKslAr8ggHzi8DrREUDbluQtNuKZ3A9PBYJZ+6z3ngqt9HmhnvRxp1SKrmlt+eQwkrGAOB0K+iiz5qNSSyy7TWvW3/RCPTb4Q1d/RAK4COtqnUS0UdEgNABd7/F2zAcKcn66rUUmhW+1OE7nVogg0iED3eeOHk=&lt;/Modulus&gt;&lt;Exponent&gt;AQAB&lt;/Exponent&gt;&lt;/RSAKeyValue&gt;</em></p><h3><span>File encryption</span></h3><p>The Paradise ransomware encrypts <strong>ALL</strong> files on fixed, removable, and network drives.</p><p>It filters out the folders that contain the following strings:</p><ul><li>windows</li><li>firefox</li><li>opera</li><li>chrome</li><li>google</li><li>The Application Data folder where the cryptolocker lives</li></ul><p>The cryptolocker does not encrypt the files that contain the following strings:</p><ul><li>.paradise</li><li>#DECRYPT MY FILES#.html</li><li>Id.dp</li><li>DecryptionInfo.auth</li></ul><p>It first encrypts the files in any folders that contain the following strings:</p><ul><li>mysql</li><li>firebird</li><li>mssql</li><li>microsoft sql</li><li>backup</li></ul><p>The cryptolocker renames a file adding the following suffix:&nbsp;\r\n“[id-&lt;USER_ID&gt;].[AFFILIATE_EMAIL].paradise”</p><p>For example:</p><p><em>file.exe[id-iO3mBQGY].[</em><a href=\"mailto:paradise@all-ransomware.info\"><em>paradise@all-ransomware.info</em></a><em>].paradise</em></p><p>Paradise uses the RSA cipher, and the generated session key pairs to the encrypt file’s content, divided in blocks of 547 bytes.</p><h3><span>Communication</span></h3><p>Once the encryption is completed, the malicious process sends a notification request to the remote server.</p><p>The sent data includes:</p><ul><li>The number of encrypted files</li><li>The computer’s name</li><li>Elapsed time</li><li>Decryption info</li><li>The computer’s ID</li></ul><p>Analyzed versions of the ransomware connect to ‘localhost’ only. The ransomware config contains ‘localhost’ as the C&amp;C server, which could mean that either the feature was deprecated or setting the server data in config was forgotten.</p><h3><span>Backup removal</span></h3><p>Paradise silently deletes Windows shadow copies, like many other ransomware variants currently in the wild:</p><h3><span>Ransom note</span></h3><p>In every folder, the cryptolocker leaves the ransom note ‘#DECRYPT MY FILES#.html’</p><h3><span>&nbsp;</span></h3><h3><span>Decryption service</span></h3><p>The ransom note includes a contact email address:</p><p><em>paradise@all-ransomware.info</em></p><p>The user can send up to three files with non-sensitive information – together with the ID and personal RSA key – to this email address to test the decryption service. Each file should be less than 1 MB in size. One of the files will be decrypted as proof that decryption is possible. The ransom value will be set in bitcoin and can vary based on when the user replies or the number of encrypted files.</p><p>The domain ‘<em>all-ransomware.info</em>’ has roots on Russia, according to WhoIs data:</p><p>The server is geographically located in St Petersburg.</p><h3><span>Conclusion</span></h3><p>There is no way to restore encrypted files other than to pay a ransom. The files are encrypted using a session public RSA key and require session private RSA key, which is encrypted along with the master public RSA key. The session RSA private key can be decrypted only with the master private RSA key, which is held by the criminals.</p><p>The only free alternative that is recommend is to restore files from backup, if available, after the infected computer has been cleaned.</p><h3><span>Acronis True Image detects and blocks Paradise as well</span></h3><p>Rather than waiting to react after Paradise encrypts your files, you can use <a href=\"https://www.acronis.com/en-us/personal/computer-backup/\">Acronis True Image 2018</a> and our other products with <a href=\"https://www.acronis.com/en-us/active-protection/\">Acronis Active Protection</a> enabled to detect and stop Paradise ransomware. You’ll also be able to restore any affected files in matter of seconds.</p>","author":{"@id":"https://www.acronis.com/#MSPThreatsSecurityTeam","name":"MSPThreatsSecurityTeam","url":"https://www.acronis.com/en/blog/authors/acronis-security-team/"},"name":"Acronis"},{"@context":"https://schema.org","@type":"BreadcrumbList","itemListElement":[{"@type":"ListItem","position":1,"name":"Acronis","item":"https://www.acronis.com/"},{"@type":"ListItem","position":2,"name":"Acronis Blog","item":"https://www.acronis.com/en/pr/"},{"@type":"ListItem","position":3,"name":"Paradise Ransomware strikes again","item":"https://www.acronis.com/en/blog/posts/paradise-ransomware-strikes-again/"}]},{"@type":"SearchAction","target":"https://www.acronis.com/en/search/?q={query}","name":"Search Action","query":"required name=query","@id":"https://www.acronis.com/en/#SearchAction"}]
</script>
    </head>

data-v-4e36c0fd></picture><!--]--></div><!----><!--]--><!----></div><figcaption class="caption" data-v-209a50b3>Paradise Ransomware hits again</figcaption></figure><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The Paradise ransomware that was active in September 2017 is back with a new round of attacks, starting at the beginning of January 2018. Leveraging the Ransomware as a Service (RaaS) model, the Paradise strain provides an unbreakable encryption scheme by using the RSA cipher for file encryption – which is an unusual cipher choice.</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The ransomware’s executable file is archived and spread via spam email as a zip attachment. To become infected, a user opens the attachment, unpacks it, and executes the extracted application.</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><div class="post-title-wrap" data-v-209a50b3><!----><h3 id="23dqAY170P" class="post-title" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>Static Analysis</span></h3></div><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The ‘DP_Main.exe’ ransomware file is a .NET compiled executable and requires .NET Framework 3.5 to start on a user’s machine (MD5: 8aa00ee509a649619794fc1390319293). The PE file is 36,684 bytes and was compiled on January 5, 2018.</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><div class="post-title-wrap" data-v-209a50b3><!----><h3 id="PbFxlm56Y9" class="post-title" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>Installation</span></h3></div><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The malware copies itself to the following folder on a user’s computer:</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3><em>C:\Users\&lt;USER&gt;\AppData\Roaming\DP\</em></span></p><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The executable adds the reference to itself in the Autorun Windows registry key as the following value:</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3><em>‘DP_Main’ = ‘c:\Users\&lt;USER&gt;\AppData\Roaming\DP\DP_Main.exe’</em></span></p><!--]--><!--[--><figure class="picture" data-v-209a50b3><div class="media-wrapper media-wrapper--screenshot" data-v-209a50b3 data-v-4b9b14eb><!--[--><div class="media screenshot-wrapper" data-v-4b9b14eb><!----><!--[--><picture class="a-picture a-media__type__screenshot full-width class="post-title-wrap" data-v-209a50b3><!----><h3 id="dDv1gTDs3x" class="post-title" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>Key generation</span></h3></div><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The <a href="https://www.acronis.com/en-us/ransomware-protection/">ransomware</a> creates ‘DecryptionInfo.auth’ file in the following folders:</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><ul class="post-list" data-v-209a50b3><!--[--><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>%USER%\</span></li><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>%USER%\Desktop\</span></li><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>&nbsp;Program Files\</span></li><!--]--></ul><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The key file contains the session RSA private key in the XML format, encrypted with the master RSA public key and Base64 encoded:</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><figure class="picture" data-v-209a50b3><div class="media-wrapper media-wrapper--screenshot" data-v-209a50b3 data-v-4b9b14eb><!--[--><div class="media screenshot-wrapper" data-v-4b9b14eb><!----><!--[--><picture class="a-picture src="https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/4524ea3e23370100e4d9818dc87cf26a.png" loading="lazy" data-v-4e36c0fd></picture><!--]--></div><!----><!--]--><!----></div><figcaption class="caption" data-v-209a50b3>Paradise Ransomware - Key generation 2</figcaption></figure><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The master RSA 1024-bit public key is hard coded in Base64:</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3><em>&lt;RSAKeyValue&gt;Modulus&gt;um4QYAdi0y8L+VKslAr8ggHzi8DrREUDbluQtNuKZ3A9PBYJZ+6z3ngqt9HmhnvRxp1SKrmlt+eQwkrGAOB0K+iiz5qNSSyy7TWvW3/RCPTb4Q1d/RAK4COtqnUS0UdEgNABd7/F2zAcKcn66rUUmhW+1OE7nVogg0iED3eeOHk=&lt;/Modulus&gt;&lt;Exponent&gt;AQAB&lt;/Exponent&gt;&lt;/RSAKeyValue&gt;</em></span></p><!--]--><!--[--><div class="post-title-wrap" data-v-209a50b3><!----><h3 id="GnHz4pmgyG" class="post-title" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>File encryption</span></h3></div><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The Paradise ransomware encrypts <strong>ALL</strong> files on fixed, removable, and network drives.</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>It filters out the folders that contain the following strings:</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><ul class="post-list" data-v-209a50b3><!--[--><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>windows</span></li><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>firefox</span></li><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>opera</span></li><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>chrome</span></li><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>google</span></li><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The Application Data folder where the cryptolocker lives</span></li><!--]--></ul><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The cryptolocker does not encrypt the files that contain the following strings:</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><ul class="post-list" data-v-209a50b3><!--[--><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>.paradise</span></li><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>#DECRYPT MY FILES#.html</span></li><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>Id.dp</span></li><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>DecryptionInfo.auth</span></li><!--]--></ul><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>It first encrypts the files in any folders that contain the following strings:</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><ul class="post-list" data-v-209a50b3><!--[--><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>mysql</span></li><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>firebird</span></li><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>mssql</span></li><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>microsoft sql</span></li><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>backup</span></li><!--]--></ul><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The cryptolocker renames a file adding the following suffix:&nbsp;
“[id-&lt;USER_ID&gt;].[AFFILIATE_EMAIL].paradise”</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>For example:</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3><em>file.exe[id-iO3mBQGY].[</em><a href="mailto:paradise@all-ransomware.info"><em>paradise@all-ransomware.info</em></a><em>].paradise</em></span></p><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>Paradise uses the RSA cipher, and the generated session key pairs to the encrypt file’s content, divided in blocks of 547 bytes.</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><figure class="picture" data-v-209a50b3><div class="media-wrapper media-wrapper--screenshot" data-v-209a50b3 data-v-4b9b14eb><!--[--><div class="media data-v-209a50b3>Paradise Ransomware - encryption</figcaption></figure><!--]--><!--[--><div class="post-title-wrap" data-v-209a50b3><!----><h3 id="LzMeQF2jqb" class="post-title" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>Communication</span></h3></div><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>Once the encryption is completed, the malicious process sends a notification request to the remote server.</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The sent data includes:</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><ul class="post-list" data-v-209a50b3><!--[--><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The number of encrypted files</span></li><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The computer’s name</span></li><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>Elapsed time</span></li><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>Decryption info</span></li><li class="post-list-item" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The computer’s ID</span></li><!--]--></ul><!--]--><!--[--><figure forgotten.</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><div class="post-title-wrap" data-v-209a50b3><!----><h3 id="gVY-UkzTJK" class="post-title" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>Backup data-v-209a50b3><!----><h3 id="4P-zbTtAVh" class="post-title" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>&nbsp;</span></h3></div><!--]--><!--[--><div class="post-title-wrap" data-v-209a50b3><!----><h3 id="Grgcwfwgv9" class="post-title" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>Decryption service</span></h3></div><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The ransom note includes a contact email address:</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3><em>paradise@all-ransomware.info</em></span></p><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The user can send up to three files with non-sensitive information – together with the ID and personal RSA key – to this email address to test the decryption service. Each file should be less than 1 MB in size. One of the files will be decrypted as proof that decryption is possible. The ransom value will be set in bitcoin and can vary based on when the user replies or the number of encrypted files.</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The domain ‘<em>all-ransomware.info</em>’ has roots on Russia, according to WhoIs data:</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><figure class="picture" data-v-209a50b3><div class="media-wrapper media-wrapper--screenshot" data-v-209a50b3 data-v-4b9b14eb><!--[--><div class="media screenshot-wrapper" data-v-4b9b14eb><!----><!--[--><picture class="a-picture a-media__type__screenshot full-width screenshot-image" type="screenshot" disablemodal="false" isoverlayclose="true" data-v-4b9b14eb data-v-4e36c0fd><!--[--><source srcset="https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/8cc965cc9d494f1b98f0d4ba67ce6dae.webp, https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content@2x/8cc965cc9d494f1b98f0d4ba67ce6dae.webp 2x" type="image/webp" data-v-4e36c0fd><source srcset="https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/8cc965cc9d494f1b98f0d4ba67ce6dae.png, https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content@2x/8cc965cc9d494f1b98f0d4ba67ce6dae.png 2x" type="image/png" data-v-4e36c0fd><!--]--><img class="a-picture__img" alt="Acronis" style="object-fit:cover;object-position:center;" src="https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/8cc965cc9d494f1b98f0d4ba67ce6dae.png" loading="lazy" data-v-4e36c0fd></picture><!--]--></div><!----><!--]--><!----></div><figcaption class="caption" data-v-209a50b3>Paradise Ransomware - domain</figcaption></figure><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The server is geographically located in St Petersburg.</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><figure class="picture" data-v-209a50b3><div class="media-wrapper media-wrapper--screenshot" data-v-209a50b3 data-v-4b9b14eb><!--[--><div class="media screenshot-wrapper" data-v-4b9b14eb><!----><!--[--><picture class="a-picture a-media__type__screenshot full-width screenshot-image" type="screenshot" disablemodal="false" isoverlayclose="true" data-v-4b9b14eb data-v-4e36c0fd><!--[--><source srcset="https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/dd62f7f5415bd0ff0d4a3b236c95052d.webp, https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content@2x/dd62f7f5415bd0ff0d4a3b236c95052d.webp 2x" type="image/webp" data-v-4e36c0fd><source srcset="https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/dd62f7f5415bd0ff0d4a3b236c95052d.png, https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content@2x/dd62f7f5415bd0ff0d4a3b236c95052d.png 2x" type="image/png" data-v-4e36c0fd><!--]--><img class="a-picture__img" alt="Acronis" style="object-fit:cover;object-position:center;" src="https://staticfiles.acronis.com/images/content/dd62f7f5415bd0ff0d4a3b236c95052d.png" loading="lazy" data-v-4e36c0fd></picture><!--]--></div><!----><!--]--><!----></div><figcaption class="caption" data-v-209a50b3>Paradise Ransomware - location</figcaption></figure><!--]--><!--[--><div class="post-title-wrap" data-v-209a50b3><!----><h3 id="dmNbU4jL0h" class="post-title" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>Conclusion</span></h3></div><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>There is no way to restore encrypted files other than to pay a ransom. The files are encrypted using a session public RSA key and require session private RSA key, which is encrypted along with the master public RSA key. The session RSA private key can be decrypted only with the master private RSA key, which is held by the criminals.</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>The only free alternative that is recommend is to restore files from backup, if available, after the infected computer has been cleaned.</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><div class="post-title-wrap" data-v-209a50b3><!----><h3 id="J0P6xXgx9x" class="post-title" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>Acronis True Image detects and blocks Paradise as well</span></h3></div><!--]--><!--[--><p class="post-paragraph" data-v-209a50b3><span class="a-dangerous-html" data-v-209a50b3>Rather than waiting to react after Paradise encrypts your files, you can use <a href="https://www.acronis.com/en-us/personal/computer-backup/">Acronis True Image 2018</a> and our other products with <a href="https://www.acronis.com/en-us/active-protection/">Acronis Active Protection</a> enabled to detect and stop Paradise ransomware. You’ll also be able to restore any affected files in matter of seconds.</span></p><!--]--><!--[--><figure class="picture" data-v-209a50b3><div class="media-wrapper media-wrapper--screenshot" Each block contains a cryptographic hash of the previous block, including a timestamp and transaction data.</p><p>Most people know the term “blockchain” because it is used as the basis for cryptocurrencies like Bitcoin or Ether. But the underlying concept allows blockchain technology to have a variety of use-cases, such as file notarization, digital voting, creating smart contracts, and more.</p><p>The key advantages of the technology includes:</p><ul><li><b>Security:</b> Blockchain uses strong cryptography to create transactions that are impervious to fraud.</li><li><b>Distributed architecture:</b> Blockchain leger is not owned by anyone as it can be distributed across multiple organizations and becomes more secure as replicas are added.</li><li><b>Impossible to backdate changes:&nbsp;</b>Every transaction is written into the ledger once and cannot be changed thereafter.</li></ul>"},{"title":"What is blockchain as a service?","content":"<p>Blockchain as a Service (BaaS) is based on the Software as a Service (SaaS) model. This approach allows customers to access and leverage blockchain-based applications, while a cloud-based service provider manages all activities required to keep the infrastructure up and running.</p>"},{"title":"What is blockchain-based data notarization?","content":"<p>Blockchain-based services for data notarization allows to notarize business critical data of any type automatically by creating a digital fingerprint for files and storing it in a public blockchain ledger. It empowers companies with independent validation of data authenticity and proof it existed at a specified date and time.</p>"},{"title":"How does e-signature work?","content":"<p>An electronic signature, or e-signature, is the software that links a signature to the signer’s identity and intent to sign to the time the document was signed. That includes family photos and videos, documents, emails, contacts, apps and even the operating system that powers your computer. If the originals are located on your laptop or a mobile device, you keep the backup somewhere else that’s safe — that way, you can use the second copy to restore your files or system if something happens to the original.</p><p>To ensure all of this data is accurately copied so you can use it to recover your computer, backup software is a must. That way, if a fire or flood damages both your original files and the local backup, the off-site copy is available to use for recovery.</p><p>\"The cloud\" is a term that describes a remote network of computers and servers that you access via the internet. That includes family photos and videos, documents, emails, contacts, apps and even the operating system that powers your computer. If the originals are located on your laptop or a mobile device, you keep the backup somewhere else that’s safe — that way, you can use the second copy to restore your files or system if something happens to the original.</p><p>To ensure all of this data is accurately copied so you can use it to recover your computer, backup software is a must. Acronis recommends the 3-2-1 backup rule, which includes storing <strong>three</strong> copies of your data on at least <strong>two</strong> different types of media (such as external hard drives, network drives, and NAS devices) and keeping <strong>one</strong> copy off-site. That way, if a fire or flood damages both your original files and the local backup, the off-site copy is available to use for recovery.</p><p>\"The cloud\" is a term that describes a remote network of computers and servers that you access via the internet. The cloud is a convenient way to store your files off-site, where they are safe from local damage.
